Last month, 2,947 people read books, 3,889 books were borrowed, 636 people borrowed books from the circulation section, 1,423 books were borrowed, 782 people read books in the mobile library, 911 books were borrowed, and 3,576 people read magazines and newspapers. A total of 7,941 people read books and 6,223 books were borrowed. According to the investigation, the museum was open for 26 days in September, excluding holidays, with an average of 304 people per day, an increase of 1,388 readers and 1,116 books read compared to August. It is also reported that the library's book catalog is being compiled and will be printed soon. This catalog will be 500 pages long, a huge volume.

Jiangsu Elementary Education Facilities (2) 36

Zhou Fohai

(2) Compiling Elementary School Curriculum Outlines and Teaching Examples for Various Subjects

At the beginning of the 22nd year, the Education Department received an order from the Ministry to compile curriculum outlines and teaching examples for various subjects in accordance with the newly promulgated kindergarten and elementary school curriculum standards. The Education Department immediately organized an editorial committee and designated Nanjing Experimental Elementary School, Nanjing Women's High School Experimental Elementary School, Suzhou High School Experimental Elementary School, Shanghai High School Experimental Elementary School, Yangzhou High School Experimental Elementary School, Songjiang Women's High School Experimental Elementary School, Zhenjiang Normal School Affiliated Elementary School, Wuxi Normal School Affiliated Elementary School, and Taizhou Normal School Affiliated Elementary School as members of the editorial committee. In addition, experts and department staff were hired to participate in the joint compilation. A total of three general meetings were held. In the first semester of the 22nd year, the provincial elementary schools compiled the first draft, which was distributed to the members for comments, and then returned to the original drafting school for correction. Finally, the overall collation was carried out. It took nearly a year to complete the compilation of all the curriculum outlines and teaching examples. The reason for the long time was that the round-trip mailing and signing took a lot of time during the compilation, and the schools responsible for the compilation mostly had their own work, so they only took a part of their time to do it. In addition, in order to adapt to the local rural elementary schools, a complex timetable and complex teaching examples for various subjects were specially formulated, which were also completed at the same time. This can be said to be the biggest contribution made by the department in conjunction with the provincial elementary schools in addition to the order from the ministry.

(3) Establishing the Dagang Rural Education Experimental Zone

We feel that the education in Jiangsu Province is too biased towards cities and neglects the countryside, resulting in a deformed development. Therefore, we also believe that the development of rural education is an urgent task. Therefore, a certain amount was allocated from the provincial education funds to establish a rural education experimental zone in Dagang, the provincial capital. The method is to integrate school education and social education and advance simultaneously. It is hoped that there will be no illiterate people and out-of-school school-age children in the area. In addition to the imparting of knowledge, the overall improvement of the countryside is also a task that should be done in the area. Special attention is paid to rural production. In the future, if considerable success is achieved, it will be prepared to be handed over to various counties for imitation. The area has now been established for one year, with a total of ten schools. Because it is slightly different from ordinary elementary schools, the center of the school's work is mostly based on meeting daily life needs, so it is called a living school. At the same time, there is also a plan for (a quarter of an hour of education), the main purpose of which is to not adopt the school's method, and to find ways to enable the public to obtain knowledge anytime and anywhere, especially in terms of literacy. Since the trial implementation, there have been considerable results.

(4) Urging Provincial Elementary Schools to Implement a New Life Without Children's Families

The implementation of the New Life Movement has been decided to start with elementary school students, using children to extend to their families, so that everyone strives to implement it and becomes a fashion. The effect is naturally easy to see. Provincial elementary schools have now formulated measures to urge children and their families to implement a new life and ordered them to comply.

(B) County-run

(1) Promoting Righteous Education Classes

Everyone knows that the compulsory education in this province is not universal. Even if we cannot extravagantly promote it due to financial difficulties, we cannot sit idly by. Therefore, taking advantage of the provincial education director's meeting, this major issue was specially handed over to them to discuss and solve the method. Because they are education administrators handling education administration in various counties in the field, the concept can be clearer and the plan set is more practical. As a result, a general outline for promoting compulsory education has been formulated and has been notified to all counties to comply with. The counties that have followed the order and prepared to promote it have a total of 1,337 classes. Although it is a drop in the bucket, it is better than nothing.

(2) Establishing Rural Township Elementary Schools

In addition to the above-mentioned general outline for promoting righteous education, another method for popularizing education was also considered, which is to order township and township autonomous personnel to strive to establish rural township elementary schools. A general outline for establishing township elementary schools has been drafted, and the provincial government has notified the county magistrates to supervise the implementation. Although most of the counties have drafted plans and submitted them for approval, due to the local economic strength, the actual number of schools established in each county throughout the year is still less than 50. It is hoped that the Ministry of Civil Affairs and the Ministry of Finance can help supervise and urge the county magistrates to strive to raise funds to establish them.

(3) Improving Private Schools

This is also an indirect method of popularizing righteous education. In fact, it can be said to be the most important method of popularizing righteous education at present. We know that the number of school-age children in each county receiving private school education is probably several times, or even dozens of times, more than those receiving school education. Although half of it is because the schools' performance is too poor to gain the trust of students' parents, the biggest reason is still that there are no schools to enter. Therefore, we

I Want to Be Quiet! The streets are not quiet. And it's freezing cold; isn't it already deep autumn? The wind is blowing at the end of October. Blowing an erotic wind. The osmanthus in the small vase is withering, the tiny blossoms covering the desk, withered, like a woman mourning the autumn. Three or five bare branches, clutching yellow leaves, peer out from the mouth of the vase, looking at their departed companions, wistful, like a poet in love lost. Last year, when the osmanthus bloomed, I bought a reddish-brown vase and a crimson incense burner. Every day, like an old woman piously praying for the repose of her husband's soul, I burned a stick of cloud incense, and spent the autumn morning in the curling smoke. The reddish-brown vase remained empty; I did not want to put flowers in it. It was a terrible cage, and I couldn't bear to see it destroy virgin flowers. Across the street is a flower shop. In the milky-white painted window, colorful bunches of flowers stand, arranged. With the window open, seeing her diminish them from her slender fingers, I look at my vase, which is empty. The sun slipped in through the window, the cloud incense was finished, and I put on my autumn coat and went out. Walking across the street, I stood outside the flower shop. The foreign woman cast a charming, smiling glance at me from behind the window, then lowered her head to knit her wool. Her fingers were slender, like those of the flower buyers. With affection for those fingers dyed with rouge, I gently pushed open the milky-white painted low door. The owner of the fingers put down her work and handed me a bunch of crimson flowers, as lovely as rouge, and I thought of the reddish-brown vase. Stumbling on the paving stones, I aligned my toe with the edge, playfully, and arrived at my workplace. The crimson flowers were generously placed in the goldfish bowl on the mantelpiece, my own fingertips not dyed with crimson rouge. The reddish-brown vase remained empty until the second autumn. When a bunch of osmanthus was placed in the vase, a pair of slender fingers dyed with rouge appeared beside the reddish-brown; the owner of the fingers leaned to my ear and said: (Bringing flowers for the flower lover.) The reddish-brown vase was still, surprised by this unexpected gift. (I don't like offering flowers!) I replied. (I do!) Like that foreign woman across the street, she cast a charming, smiling glance. Who is the owner of this reddish-brown vase? The osmanthus has withered, autumn is old. Smoke drifts from the crimson incense burner. The reddish-brown vase is empty again, wait for the arrival of the third autumn! Paying attention to my own fingers, not dyed with crimson rouge. Occasionally glancing across the street, in the milky-white painted window, flowers diminish from slender fingers. That foreign woman lowers her head and knits her wool. At the corner of the road, the pinkish-red light in the glass case shines with the streetlights, illuminating the plump chickens and ducks hanging there and the strips of roast meat, adding a layer of bluish light to the roasted red skin. The aroma wafts out of the case and spreads onto the sidewalk. People passing by cannot help but turn their heads to look at the meat and chickens because of the waves of fragrance. A boy in his teens comes strolling over, shrugging his shoulders, his hands tightly clasped across his chest, trying to reduce the torment of the wind. Barefoot, he drags his worn-out shoes. His pants are torn so badly you can see half his butt. His top has no collar. His hair is long, and his face is as thin as a monkey's. The boy stops outside the glass case. The pinkish-red light casts a blue glow on his face, making him look even less human. He tugs at the corner of his tattered clothes. His eyes stare straight at the chickens and meat. The moisture in his mouth suddenly increases, almost overflowing, so he tries desperately to swallow it down his throat, but the more he swallows, the more there is. Finally, he wipes his lips with his filthy sleeve. The clock hanging in the shop chimes six times, and the sweet sound startles the boy, who is standing there blankly. (It's time for supper!) he thinks. He looks up at the dark sky, then wipes his lips again with his hand. The lure of the chickens and meat hanging in the case becomes even greater, and the aroma is even stronger. He looks at the luscious food, and his stomach rumbles. He unconsciously presses his hand on his abdomen, loosens his belt, and then tightens it again. (Two pennies' worth of sliced roast!) A customer throws two coppers onto the chopping board. The shop assistant takes a piece of meat from the glass case, cuts off a slice, wraps it up, and hands it to the customer. After the customer leaves, the shop assistant finds some meat scraps on the chopping board, scrapes them up with his knife, and throws them on the ground. The boy outside the case smacks his lips and sighs softly. (Why can't I have even a few scraps of meat to eat?) he wonders. He looks at the other people, then looks at himself. Don't they all have mouths and stomachs too? His feet are getting tired, so he leans lightly against the glass case. The meat and chickens are only separated from him by a layer of glass. (If there were no glass...) he thinks. (Damn it!) the shop assistant inside the case yells, glaring. He straightens up quickly and walks away hesitantly. He wipes his mouth again with his sleeve and disappears into the crowd. The aroma continues to spread on the sidewalk, the chickens, that meat... The Heart of the Seasons... Autumn seems like a woman who has lost her love. Spring is a young girl, she has vitality, lively, full of the power of vigor, full of the phenomenon of striving, beautiful, healthy, lovely, making people feel the desire for life! Not like autumn. Summer is a timely young woman, she has enthusiasm, fiery, full of hope, illusions, golden dreams. She makes people feel the necessity of life, the joy of progress, everything is warm and exciting, striving, the kind of spirit of moving forward. Not like autumn. Not like spring. It is completely like summer itself. Winter is a solemn widow, she has senility, gloomy and silent, declining, full of the pain of the remaining years, full of old age and solemnity, full of intense crisis, full of unbearable, unfeeling, cold, lacking friendly enthusiasm. Winter is too simple, too bleak, too withered, too much making people feel the sorrow of the end. Winter is not like spring, not like autumn, and not like summer. I am not happy with summer, I do not like winter, I do not approve of spring, and I do not miss autumn! I wish, that there were all four seasons, spring, summer, autumn, and winter, that kind of mixed weather. Amateur Mailbox Legal Businesses are Protected Editor: I have an uncle who has been doing business in America for over ten years. Six years ago, he returned to China and, in a rural town, jointly established a bank, with my uncle serving as manager. Over the years, it has made a profit of more than 20,000 yuan. Recently, due to the influence of the environment, a sudden panic arose, and all current and term deposits were withdrawn. The bank was temporarily unable to cope and had to suspend operations. Being defeated, there is originally no pain to speak of. However, what is most infuriating is that one of the shareholders, wanting to seize the position of manager, used vicious means to wantonly destroy and oppress, limiting my uncle to hand over his unmatured long-term deposit within the shortest possible period, or else he would kill my uncle's entire family. The bank has now resumed operations a month ago, and all current and long-term deposits have been cleared. However, as the bank is not registered with the government, can the defamation and intimidation be brought to court? What method can be used to prosecute? I hope for a prompt response. Sincerely, and wishing you good health. Kang Ye Editor's Note: Kang Ye's letter contains abstract descriptions, making it difficult to provide a specific answer. However, since the person has funds deposited in the bank, they can naturally withdraw them. If there is actual defamation or intimidation of life and property that endangers public safety, legal action can be taken, and the local police should be notified at any time. As for unregistered businesses, it seems difficult to seek legal protection for their shop names unless they are intentionally infringed upon. However, for common issues such as business operations and property, they still enjoy legal protection, which is unrelated to being unregistered. Shipping Radio (1180) Zhang Mengfei's Zen Lyrics 1:00 PM to 1:45 PM Opening: Meng Yuehua Shelters from Rain at the Imperial Stele Pavilion Yuehua is the shadow of the setting sun, hurrying along. Who knew that a sudden storm would rise in the sky? The rustling sound grew more intense. Eventually, yellow dust filled the sky. Watching the children's kite string break, it disappeared in an instant. Hearing the trees by the roadside rustling, the wind was fierce as it entered the bamboo forest. It blew the boat against the current to shore. It blew the sail of the boat with the wind to the edge. It blew the long willow leaves to sleep and wake again. It blew the powerless willow catkins to the west and east. Moreover, dark clouds obscured the sky in an instant, the scenery was dim as dusk. Suddenly hearing the temple bell shatter her heart, it turned out that the thunder was rumbling non-stop. Lightning was ten thousand golden snakes dancing in the sky, like a rainbow hanging in the middle of the sky. It was clear that the Rain Master and the Wind Earl had come to meet, so they instructed the Thunder God and Lightning Mother to be the vanguard. At this time, there were few people in the open fields, Meng Yuehua could not stop her heart from pounding. Moreover, the cool breeze made her clothes feel thin and the spring cold tender. Suddenly looking up, the drizzle was misty. Seeing all the pedestrians avoiding the rain and going home, Yuehua was at her wits' end. Her body was as soft as cotton and without strength. Automotive Anecdotes Pei American Bandit Praises Ford's Superior Speed Dillinger was a notorious American bandit. He was killed by police officers in Chicago on July 22 of this year. However, his name has already caused a sensation among men and women all over America. Everyone regards him as a very mysterious bandit. His deeds have almost all been used as material for conversation. His greatest skill during his lifetime was robbing banks and escaping from prison. Here is a letter he wrote to automobile king Ford during his lifetime, which is now regarded as a good story in the local area of Quilo. Dillinger's letter said, "Dear Mr. Ford, I want to thank you for manufacturing such an excellent car. If I am arrested, then the people who arrest me will definitely be in a Ford car. John Dillinger (signed)" This letter was received by Ford on July 17. At first, he thought someone was deliberately joking. It was not until Dillinger was killed and the police officers verified the handwriting that he realized that the letter was actually written by the bandit himself. This letter was sent from Minnebalis (Minnesota), and at that time, the reports said that Dillinger was hiding in Illinois, Indiana, and Michigan. As for why Dillinger praised Ford, it was because he had used Ford to escape from several very dangerous situations. The most famous was in Crown Point, Indiana. He used a fake gun made of wood to escape from the prison. Chrysler Automobile Reaches One Million Units The famous Chrysler automobile has reached one million units in the past seven years. In 1931, the floating engine frame was invented and applied. At that time, Chrysler jumped to third place in the automobile industry. This position has not declined to this day. However, they will still retain the original style. As for the aspect of progress, we can have no worries. The automobile business is always moving forward, and the progress in social and economic aspects is the same as in the past," and so on. On the (Security Measures) in the Revised Draft of the Criminal Law Ting · 37

In recent days, the Legislative Yuan in the capital has been discussing the revised draft of the Criminal Law with great enthusiasm. After a general review of the contents of this draft, we believe that it contains many improvements over the existing law. However, it is not without its debatable points. Due to space limitations, we cannot discuss them in detail. We will only focus on the most noteworthy Chapter 12 (Security Measures).

Chapter 12 (Security Measures) of the revised draft has already passed its second reading in the Legislative Yuan and will soon begin its third reading. It is expected that the implementation of (Security Measures) will result in a dualistic system in the new Criminal Law, that is, those deemed typical will be subject to criminal penalties, while atypical individuals (such as boys and girls under the age of fourteen and people with mental illness) will be subject to (Security Measures). This intention stems from the doctrine of social defense, which aims to make offenders useful members of society again. However, progressive liberals today believe that (Security Measures) are still a form of criminal sanction. The rights and freedoms of those subject to the measures are inevitably deprived, and they experience suffering. In essence, there is no significant difference between being subject to these measures and being punished by law. It is also said that the prerequisite for punishment is that the offender must be capable of accepting it. If young people under the age of fourteen and people with mental illness do not have sufficient cognitive ability, then forcing them to accept the measures is ineffective. Although those who advocate this view today may inevitably feel that their voices are not widely heard, it cannot be said that they have no insight. Therefore, when a judge announces (Security Measures), they must carefully consider the individual's freedom. The procedures applied by the court must also be meticulously strict and differ from ordinary criminal proceedings. The revised draft's provisions on (Security Measures) include (1) the rehabilitation and education of juvenile offenders; (2) the guardianship of mentally ill offenders; (3) the prohibition of opium or other substitute drug use and offenses committed due to alcoholism; and (4) the forced labor of habitual offenders. The nature of these four measures varies considerably. Therefore, to ensure the consistency of principles in criminal law, it is necessary to promulgate and implement various special single-line regulations in conjunction with the law. Otherwise, if it is merely empty talk and only seeks embellishment on paper, what good will it do in practice? Articles 30 and 31 of the current Criminal Law also contain provisions on (Security Measures), but their effect is almost nil because the state's facilities for compulsory rehabilitation and education of juvenile offenders and guardianship and treatment of mentally ill offenders are not yet perfect. In order to learn from past mistakes, we cannot help but hope that the government authorities and the members of the Criminal Law Committee of the Legislative Yuan will continue their efforts.

Furthermore, the (Security Measures) and (Probation) in the revised draft have been merged into one chapter, and the implementation of (Probation) can only be determined at the discretion of the judge. Even if the judge grants approval, its meaning is limited to supplementing the effect of criminal penalties and cannot directly replace criminal penalties. Therefore, in the midst of leniency, there is still a suspicion of overly strict legislation, which is somewhat contrary to the overall spirit of this revision. Furthermore, according to Article 92 of the revised draft, (Probation is to be carried out by police stations, self-governing bodies, charitable organizations, the person's closest relatives, or other appropriate persons.) The scope is undoubtedly broad. It is not inappropriate for the closest relatives of juvenile offenders to be responsible for their rehabilitation and education, but the situation of mentally ill offenders and offenders who use opium or other substitute drugs should be treated differently. The state should not only find ways to provide passive guardianship for these two types of offenders, but also active treatment. In today's China, local self-governing bodies and charitable organizations rarely have such treatment facilities, and the same is true for private families. Therefore, the state's burden is particularly heavy, and it is ultimately impossible to shirk responsibility. If the Criminal Law only makes a general provision for the delivery of (Probation) without distinguishing the nature of the persons under supervision, then the mentally ill offender may find it difficult to recover quickly, and the opium or other drug addict may be permanently trapped in misery due to the protection of his or her closest relatives, unable to extricate themselves. The result is contrary to the original intention. Is this not a case of harming the person one loves? This is another point that must be urgently corrected.

The Executive Yuan Passes the Method of Public Servants Donating Salaries to Aid Disaster Relief 38

And Resolves to Strictly Investigate the Case of Stealing and Transporting Antiques

(Nanjing) The Executive Yuan held its 183rd meeting at 9:00 a.m. on the 23rd. More than 20 people attended, including Wang Zhaoming, Kong Xiangxi, Chen Gongbo, Chen Shaokuan, Zhu Jiahua, Wang Shijie, Chen Shuren, Shi Qingyang, Liu Ruiheng, Gan Naiguang, Fu Rulin, Xu Mo, Tang Youren, Qin Fen, Zou Lin, Zeng Zhongming, Duan Xipeng, Chu Minyi, and Peng Xuepei. Premier Wang chaired the meeting, and the following important cases were resolved:

(A) Reporting Items

(1) Huang Fu, Chairman of the Commission for the Reorganization of Political Affairs in Beiping, telegraphed to report the organizational outline of the War Zone Clearance Commission and planned to announce the establishment of the War Zone Clearance Commission on October 25th of this year. The candidates for the commissioners were to be designated by the Commission, the Beiping Branch of the Military Affairs Commission, the governments of Hebei and Chahar provinces, and the Jiji and Luan Yu administrative supervisors. The case was approved by the Yuan and telegraphed for record.

(2) Liu Xiang, Commander-in-Chief of the Bandit Suppression in Sichuan, telegraphed on the 22nd to report that he had been ordered to suppress bandits, but had not succeeded after the deadline. He had repeatedly telegraphed requesting to be relieved of his concurrent posts, but had not been approved. He had received frequent warm exhortations and had immediately rushed to Chengdu and respectfully resumed his post on October 22nd. He telegraphed requesting to be informed of the case. The Yuan has replied by telegram to encourage him.

(B) Examination and Reporting Items

(1) Minister Huang of the Ministry of Interior and Minister Kong of the Ministry of Finance reported that they had been instructed to examine the case submitted by the Ministry of Interior regarding the revised Provisional Regulations for Land Registration in the Land Survey Area of Henan Province. The examination opinion was that the proposed revision of the regulations, the cancellation of the detailed rules, and the forms used were generally appropriate. However, there were still some amendments to be made to the revised articles. The opinion was submitted along with the proposed amendments for consideration. The decision was to pass the examination opinion.

(2) Minister Huang of the Ministry of Interior and concurrently Minister Wang of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs reported that they had been instructed to examine the case submitted by the Ministry of Interior requesting the revision of the Nationality Law and its implementing regulations. The examination opinion was that the Ministry of Interior's proposal to supplement the Nationality Law by adding (The wife and children of a person who loses nationality shall not lose nationality with him or her) as the second paragraph after the original text of Article 11 of the Law was feasible. The proposed revisions to the articles of the implementing regulations were also generally appropriate, but there were some points that needed to be slightly revised. The opinion was submitted along with the revised opinion for consideration. The decision was to pass the revision and consult the Legislative Yuan.

(C) Decisions on Appointments and Removals

(1) Minister He of the Ministry of Military Affairs submitted a request to appoint Feng Zirang as the Director of the Medical Department of the 47th Division. Passed.

(2) Ma Heng, Director of the Beiping Palace Museum, submitted a request to appoint Zhang Tingji as the Secretary of the Museum and Huang Nianqu as the Section Chief. Passed.

(D) Discussion Items

(1) Minister Kong of the Ministry of Finance proposed that a method be stipulated for public servants to donate their salaries and to issue a general order to all agencies inside and outside the capital to implement it uniformly. From October of this year to March of next year, all public servants with a monthly salary of 50 yuan or more should donate 1 yuan, those with 100 yuan or more should donate 2 yuan, and for every additional 50 yuan, the donation should be increased by 1 yuan. The accounting personnel of each agency should be responsible for deducting the amount monthly and remitting it to the Executive Yuan for allocation and use to relieve disaster victims. Please make a public decision. The decision was passed and sent to the Secretariat of the Central Political Conference for transmission. (2) Minister Zhu of the Ministry of Transportation requested that Article 4 of the Provisional Regulations for Applying for Wireless Electrical Material Transit Permits be amended to require that the aforementioned materials be subject to inspection by military police, customs, and mine clearance bureau personnel in various places to facilitate implementation. Please consider and forward it for record. The decision was passed.

(3) Minister Kong of the Ministry of Finance requested that Article 13 of the Organizational Law of the Central Mint be amended. Please consider the case. The decision was passed and sent to the Legislative Yuan.

(4) It was resolved to order the Central Antiquities Preservation Committee to strictly investigate the case of stealing and replacing jewelry and stealing and transporting antiques in the Palace Museum. (Central News Agency telegram, 23rd)

England-Australia Air Race The English Comet Wins the Championship 52

Completing Over 11,000 Miles in Two Days and Twenty-Three Hours

Prize Money of £10,000 Readily Available

The Netherlands is Second and the United States is Third

Melbourne English aviators Scott and Black arrived in Melbourne at 5:34 a.m. this morning and landed at Laverton Airfield, winning the championship.

Dutch aviators Parmentier and Moll flew from Darwin to Melbourne at 10:00 a.m. this morning. They have now safely landed at the Albury Racecourse in Melbourne, taking second place.

American aviators Turner and Pangborn flew to Charlie Town at 8:42 a.m. this morning, which is 767 miles from Melbourne, and are expected to be in third place. (Reuters telegram, 23rd)

Melbourne English aviators Scott and Black safely landed here on the victorious plane at 5:34 a.m. this morning. The crowds participating in the centenary celebration gave a tumultuous welcome to the winning team of the England-Australia air race. It took some effort for the exhausted aviators to break through the encirclement and go to the hotel for a rest. The two aviators flew at a speed of 160 miles per hour. The engine of their plane was damaged in the middle of the journey, which was the reason for their delay in reaching their destination by several hours. The air race committee announced that their official landing time was 5:34:48 a.m. (Greenwich time) and their official departure time was 6:34:30 a.m., setting a new record for the entire journey from London to Melbourne in 71 hours and 18 minutes. The flight time was two days and twenty-three hours, with an average speed of 160 miles per hour, securing the speed flight championship of 50,000 US dollars. It is not yet certain whether they will also win the obstacle flight championship of 10,000 US dollars. (National telegram, 23rd)

The Crowd Welcomed Enthusiastically 53

Melbourne The Comet aircraft of English aviators Scott and Black landed at the airfield here at 5:43 a.m. this morning (Greenwich time), flying 11,323 miles in two days, twenty-two hours, fifty-nine minutes, and fifty seconds, winning the championship in the unprecedented England-Australia air race in aviation history. Thousands of spectators in the field cheered when they saw the Comet circling down. After Scott and Black landed, two Australian female aviators immediately approached and presented them with two bottles of beer and two sandwiches. Scott and Black walked out of the plane, temporarily deafened and unable to hear the cheers, but both had smiles on their faces and waved to the crowd. They were led by friends to the hangar and provided with refreshments. After five minutes, they returned to the field.

Home
